Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[(Brahman.тАФ─Бdhy─Бtmam; rohit─Бdityadevatyam. tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham.) 1. 4-av. 5-p. ─Бkс╣Ыti; 2-4. 3-av. 6-p. (2, 3. aс╣гс╣нi, 2. bhurij; 4. ati┼Ы─Бkvaragarbh─Б dhс╣Ыti); 5-7. 4-av. 7-p. (5, 6. ┼Ы─Бkvar─Бti┼Ы─Бkvaragarbh─Б prakс╣Ыti; 7. anuс╣гс╣нubgarbk─Б тАЩtidhс╣Ыti); 8. 3-av. 6-p. atyaс╣гс╣нi; 9-19. 4-av. (9-12, 15, 17. 7-p. bhurig atidhс╣Ыti, 15. nicс╣Ыt, 17. kс╣Ыti; 13, 14, 16, 18, 19. 8-p., 13, 14. vikс╣Ыti, 16, 18, 19. ─Бkс╣Ыti, 19. bhurij); 20, 22. 3-av. 6-p. atyaс╣гс╣нi; 21, 23-25. 4-av. 8-p. (24. 7-p. kс╣Ыti; 21. ─Бkс╣Ыti; 24, 25. vikс╣Ыti).]*

Whitney

Comment

Of this hymn only one verse is found in P─Бipp., namely vs. 10 in iv. V─Бit. makes use of no part of it; and K─Бu┼Ы. тМК49. 19тМЛ only of the first verse. тМКCaland, p. 173, understands the whole hymn to be intended at 49. 19; and takes 49. 24 and 25 as referring to vss. 6 and 7 of this hymn.тМЛ *тМКThe definition of vs. 26 (anuс╣гс╣нubh) appears to be omitted.тАФThe individual p─Бdas of this hymn are largely of genuine triс╣гс╣нubh measure and cadence, occasionally jagat─л; and this is possibly the intention of the “tr─Бiс╣гс╣нubham” of the Anukr. (for not a single verse foots up as 44 syllables): then, again, if to the verse proper in each case we add the refrain and reckon up the totals, we get the ─Бkс╣Ыtis etc. of the Anukr.тМЛ

Translations

Translated: Ludwig, p. 543; Henry, 14, 45; Deussen, Geschichte, i. 1. 226; Griffith, ii. 150.

Griffith

A glorification of Rohita. with a malediction on the man who wrongs a Brahman

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who generated these two, heaven-and-earth; who clothes himself in
    existences, making them a garment (dr─Б╠Бpi); in whom abide the six wide
    directions, toward which he, the flying one, looks all abroadтАФagainst
    that god, angered, [is] this offense (─Б╠Бgas); whoso scathes a Brahman
    that knows thus, do thou, O ruddy one, make him quake, destroy him;
    fasten on the fetters of the Brahman-scather.
Notes

All the mss. agree in the accent of dr─Б╠Бpi (RV. always dr─Бp├н). As is
their habit, they give of the refrain only the single word t├бsya
except in vss. 1 and 25; and there they set the avas─Бna not before
t├бsya, but after dev├бsya: in our edition this perversion of the
natural division is corrected. The refrain, if we contract y├б ev├бm to
y─Б├н тАЩv├бm, is a regular triс╣гс╣нubh; its addition to a preceding verse
makes this hymn one of especially long meters; the first verse, 8 p─Бdas
of 11 syllables each, is an exact ─Бkс╣Ыti. The verse тМКor the hymn: see
introductionтМЛ is (though v. 12. 9 has the same prat─лka) doubtless the
one quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 49. 19, with xiii. 1. 28 and xvi. 6. 1, to accompany
the laying on of fetters; and Bloomfield suggests that the whole hymn
(or anuv─Бka) is intended also in 63. 21, one does not see why.

Griffith

He who engendered these, the earth and heaven, who made the worlds the mantle that he weareth, In whom abide the six wide-spreading regions through which the Bird’s keen vision penetrateth, This God is wroth offended by the sinner who wrongs the Brahman who hath gained this knowledge Agitate him, O Rohita; destroy him: entangle in thy snares the Braman’s tyrant.

Whitney
Translation
  1. From whom the winds in their season go purifying (p┼л), out of whom
    the oceans flow forthтАФagainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

With b compare 1. 42 d. The verse (10 + 11: 44 = 65) has one
more syllable than a regular aс╣гс╣нi, as the Anukr. notices. тМКThe longer
grammatical equivalent of v─Б╠Бt─Бs would improve the rhythm.тМЛ

Griffith

He from whom winds blow pure in ordered season, from whom the seas flow forth in all directions, This God, etc.

Who with the breath he draws sates earth and heaven, with expiration fills the ocean’s belly, This God, etc.

    V─Бi┼Ыv─Бnara with the series (pan╠Дkt├н); who took to himself the breath of

    etc.
Notes

We had nearly the same combination of divine personages above in viii.
5. 10 c, d; and the pan╠Дkti here perhaps corresponds to the ‘all
the seers’ there. The verse, of very irregular meter (12 + 12: 15: 44 =
83), is very nearly a prakс╣Ыti (84 syll.).

Griffith

In whom Viraj, Prajapati, Parameshthin, Agni Vaisvanara abide with Pankti, He who hath taken to himself the breathing of the Supreme, the vigour of the Highest, This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Upon whom are set (┼Ыrit├б) the six wide [spaces], the five
    quarters, the four waters, the three syllables (? akс╣г├бra) of the
    sacrifice; who, angered, looked with his eye between the two firmaments
    (r├│daс╣г─л)тАФagainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

All our mss. read at end of b akс╣г├бr─Б (not -r─Бс╕е), doubtless under
the influence of the ordinary use of akс╣г├бra as neuter. The omission in
c of c─Бkс╣гuс╣г─Б would better both sense and meter. The verse as best
read (12 + 12: 14: 44 = 82) lacks two syllables of a full prakс╣Ыti, but
could easily be filled up by resolution. тМКFor the transition -t after
y├бsmin, cf. Pr─Бt. ii. 9 note.тМЛ тМКCaland, p. 173, understands this vs.
and the following to be intended at K─Бu┼Ы. 49. 24, 25, for use in the
ceremony of the “water-thunderbolts”: cf. introd. to x. 5.тМЛ

Griffith

On whom rest six expenses and five regions, four waters, and three syllables of worship, He who hath looked between both spheres in anger, This God, etc.

The verse (6 ├Ч 11 = 66) lacks two syllables of a full atyaс╣гс╣нi (68
syll.).

Griffith

He who metes out the thirteenth month, constructed with days and nights, containing thirty members, This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Black the descent, the yellow eagles, clothing themselves in waters,
    fly up to the sky; they have come hither from the seat of
    righteousnessтАФagainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The first three p─Бdas are RV. i. 164. 47 a-c, found also twice
above, as vi. 22. 1; ix. 10. 22. The verse (7 ├Ч 11 = 77) is accurately
described by the Anukr. It, with a good part of those that follow
(11-16, 18-21, 23, 25), appears to have nothing to do with the refrain.

Griffith

Dark the descent; the strong-winged birds are golden: they fly aloft to heaven, enrobed in waters. They have come hither from the seat of Order, This God, etc.

What silver. Kasyapa, thou hast refulgent, what brightly-shining lotus-flower collected, Wherein are gathered seven Suns together, This God, etc.

Notes
Griffith

In front the Brihat-Saman is his mantle, and from behind Rathantara enfolds him, Ever with care robing themselves in splendour. This God, etc.

резрей рд╕ рд╡рд░реБрдгрдГ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. This Agni becomes Varuс╣Зa in the evening; in the morning, rising, he
    becomes Mitra; he, having become Savitar, goes through the atmosphere;
    he, having become Indra, burns (tap) through the midst of the
    sky.тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

Or (a) ‘he becomes Varuс╣Зa at evening [and] Agni’ (so Henry: cf.
Ludwig). The verse is very irregular, but can be made to count a
vikс╣Ыti (92 syll.).

Griffith

At evening he is Varuna and Agni, ascending in the morning he is Mitra. As Savitar, he moves through air’s mid region, as Indra warms- the heavens from the centre. This God, etc.

резрек рд╕рд╣рд╕реНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдгреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдпрддрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдп ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. A thousand days’ journey are expanded the wings of him, of the
    yellow swan flying to heaven; he, putting all the gods in his breast,
    goes viewing together all existences.тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The verse proper here is a repetition of x. 8. 18 and xiii. 2. 38; it is
written in full in all the mss., because they have no other way of
indicating the attachment here of the refrain. It is properly an ─Бkс╣Ыti
(8 ├Ч 11 = 88 syll.).

Griffith

This gold-hued Harisa’s wings, soaring to heaven spread o’er a thousand days’ continued journey. Supporting all the Gods upon his bosom, he goes his way behol- ding every creature. This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Swift-running yellow [horses] draw the bright one (┼Ыukr├б), the
    god shining with splendor in the sky, whose lofty bodies heat the sky;
    hitherward with well-colored gleams (? paс╣нar├б) he shines
    forth.тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

Our edition ought to give in c tanv├аs, since that is the
pada-reading, and it is only by accident that nearly all the
saс╣Бhit─Б-mss. (all save R.K.) unite in protracting the ├а to ─Б╠А. The
verse reads most naturally as a bhurig ─Бkс╣Ыti (12 + ll: l1 + 11: 44 =
89).

Griffith

With flying feet his tawny coursers carry the bright God through, the sky, aglow with splendour. Whose limbs uplifted fire and heat the heavens: hither he shines- with beams of golden colour. This God, etc.

Griffith

He beside whom his bay steeds bear the Adityas, by whom as sacrifice go many knowing. The sole light shining spread through various places. This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Seven harness a one-wheeled chariot; one horse, having seven names,
    draws [it]; of three naves [is] the wheel, unwasting, unassailed,
    whereon stand all these existences.тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

We had the verse (which is RV. i. 164. 2) above as ix. 9. 2. The mss.
all give it in full here (as in the case of vs. 14 above).

Griffith

This seven make the one-wheeled chariot ready: bearing seven names the single courser draws it. The wheel, three-naved, is sound and undecaying: thereon these worlds of life are all dependent. This God, etc.

    g─Бyatr─л╠Б, the womb (embryo?) of the immortal.тАФAgainst that god etc.

syll.).

Griffith

Whitney
Translation
  1. Three settings, dawnings also three; three welkins, skies verily
    three: we know, O Agni, the birth-place of thee threefold; threefold the
    births of the gods we know.тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The verse is regular if tredh─Б╠Б in c (not in d) is made, as
often elsewhere, trisyllabic.

Griffith

There are the settings, three the upward risings, three are the- spaces, yea, and three the heavens. We know thy triple place of birth, O Agni, we know the deities’’ triple generations.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who in birth (j─Б╠Бyam─Бna) opened out the earth, [who] set the
    ocean in the atmosphereтАФagainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The meter is the same as that of vs. 20.

Griffith

He who, as soon as born, laid broad earth open, and set the ocean in the air’s mid-region, This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Thou, O Agni, impelled by powers (kr├бtu), by lights (ket├║),
    didst shine up, a kindled song (? ark├б) in the sky; unto what did the
    Maruts, having the spotted one for mother, sing, when the gods generated
    the ruddy one?тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

Pischel (Ved. Stud. i. 26) takes ark├б as ‘sun’; the connection with
abhy ─Бrcan in c is strongly opposed to this. The last p─Бda is the
same with 12 c above. The verse (12 + 12: 12 + 11: 44) counts
properly 91 syllables, one short of a full vikс╣Ыti.

Griffith

Thou, Agni, kind with lights and mental powers, hast up in heaven shone as the Sun, enkindled. The Maruts, sons of Prisni, sang his praises what time the Gods gave Rohita his being. This God, etc.

реирек рдп рдЖрддреНрдорджрд╛ ...{Loading}...
Whitney
Translation
  1. He who is self-giving, strength-giving, of whom all, of whom
    [even] the gods wait upon the direction, who is master of these
    bipeds, who of quadrupedsтАФagainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The verse proper is identical with the first three p─Бdas of iv. 2. 1
(found also in other texts: see the notes to that hymn). Bp. here reads
(doubtless by accident) asya in c. Two more syllables are needed
to make a full kс╣Ыti (80 syll.).

Griffith

Giver of breath, giver of strength and vigour, he whose com- mandment all the Gods acknowledge, He who is Lord of this, of man and cattle, This God, etc.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The one-footed strode out more than the two-footed; the two-footed
    falls upon the three-footed from behind; the four-footed acted within
    the call of the two-footed ones, beholding the series (pan╠Дt├н), drawing
    near (upa-sth─Б).тАФAgainst that god etc. etc.
Notes

The first two p─Бdas are identical with 2. 27 a, b, and the whole
verse corresponds to RV. X. 117. 8. RV. reads in a bh┼л╠Бyo dvip├бdo,
in b dvip─Б╠Бt trip─Б╠Бdam, in c eti (for cakre) dvip├бd─Бm, in
d pan╠Дkt─л╠Бr up-. The accentuation dv├нp─Бt and tr├нp─Бt (only in
these verses) was noticed under 2. 27. Here we lack two syllables of a
full vikс╣Ыti.

Griffith

The single-footed hath outstepped the biped, the biped overtakes the triple-footed. The quadruped hath wrought when bipeds called him, standing and looking on the five collected. This God is wroth offended by the sinner that wrongs the Brahman who hath gained this knowledge. Agitate him, O Rohita; destroy him: entangle in thy snares the Brahman’s tyrant.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The white son of the black [mother], the young of night, was born;
    he ascends upon the sky; the ruddy one ascended the ascents.
Notes

тМКHere ends the third anuv─Бka, with 1 hymn and 26 verses. The quoted
Anukr. says с╣гaс╕Нviс╣Е┼Ыat (с╣гaс╕Нviс╣Е┼Ыa?).тМЛ

Griffith

Born is the darksome Mother’s Son, the whitely shining Calf of Night. He, Rohita, ascendeth up to heaven, hath mounted to the heights.

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ) рдХреГрд╖реНрдг рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓реА (рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐ рд╕реЗ [рдкреНрд░рд▓рдп рдХреА рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐ рдХреЗ рдкреАрдЫреЗ] (рдкреБрддреНрд░рдГ) рд╢реБрджреНрдз рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛, (рдЕрд░реНрдЬреБрдирдГ) рд░рд╕ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ (рд╡рддреНрд╕рдГ) рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп [рдЬрд┐рд╕ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдпрдо рд╕реЗ] (рдЕрдЬрд╛рдпрдд) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рд╣реБрдЖ рд╣реИред (рд╕рдГ рд╣) рд╡рд╣реА (рд░реЛрд╣рд┐рддрдГ) рд╕рдмрдХрд╛ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд░рдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓рд╛ [рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░] (рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдзрд┐) рдЙрд╕ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдореЗрдВ (рд░реЛрд╣рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯ рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ, рдЙрд╕ рдиреЗ (рд░реБрд╣рдГ) рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдХреА рд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░рд┐рдпреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рд░реБрд░реЛрд╣) рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИ реереиремрее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬрд┐рд╕ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рдХреЗ рдирд┐рдпрдо рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд▓рдп рдХреЗ рдкреАрдЫреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЖрджрд┐ рд▓реЛрдХ рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рд╣реЛрддреЗ рд╣реИрдВ, рдордиреБрд╖реНрдп рдЙрд╕рдХреА рдЖрд░рд╛рдзрдирд╛ рдХрд░ рдХреЗ рд╕рджрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦреА рд░рд╣реЗрдВ реереиремреердЗрд╕ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдХрд╛ рдЪреМрдерд╛ рдкрд╛рдж рдЖ рдЪреБрдХрд╛ рд╣реИ-рдЕреж ┬Чрезрейредрезредрек рее рдЗрддрд┐ рддреГрддреАрдпреЛрд╜рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рее

рдкрдгреНрдбрд┐рдд рдХреНрд╖реЗрдордХрд░рдгрджрд╛рд╕ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реЗрджреА - рдкрд╛рджрдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдгреА: реиремтИТ(рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ) рдХреГрд╖реНрдгрд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ (рдкреБрддреНрд░рдГ) рдкреБрд╡реЛ рд╣реНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рд╢реНрдЪред рдЙреж рекредрезремрелред рдкреВрдЮреН рд╢реЛрдзрдиреЗтИТрдХреНрддреНрд░ред рд╢реЛрдзрдХрдГ (рдЕрд░реНрдЬреБрдирдГ) рд░рд╕рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╣реАрддрд╛ (рд░рд╛рддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рдГ) рдкреНрд░рд▓рдп-рд░рд╛рддреНрд░рд┐рдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ (рд╡рддреНрд╕рдГ) рд╡рд╕ рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕реЗ-рд╕ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГред рдирд┐рд╡рд╛рд╕рд╣реЗрддреБрдГ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХрдГ (рдЕрдЬрд╛рдпрдд) рдкреНрд░рдХрдЯреЛрд╜рднрд╡рддреН (рд╕рдГ) (рд╣) рдПрд╡ (рджреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрдзрд┐) рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ (рд░реЛрд╣рддрд┐) рдкреНрд░рд╛рджреБрд░реНрднрд╡рддрд┐ (рд░реБрд╣рдГ) рдЕреж резрейредрезредрекред рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реАрдГ (рд░реБрд░реЛрд╣) рдЬрдирдпрд╛рдорд╛рд╕ (рд░реЛрд╣рд┐рддрдГ) рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХрдГ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдГ рее
